Copper substituted P2-type Na0.67CuxMn1-xO2: a stable high-power sodium-ion battery cathode. J. Mater. Chem. A 3, 22846–22852 (2015)." href="/articles/s41467-021-22523-3#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d1718850e2254">45</a></sup>. <b>c</b> Cycle performance of Na<sub>0.612</sub>K<sub>0.056</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> and Na<sub>0.706</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> at 50 mA g<sup>−1</sup>. <b>d</b> Variation of <i>D</i><sub>Na</sub> + as functions of x in Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>K<sub>0.056</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> determined by GITT and CV, where the gray dotted area represents the two-phase region. <b>e</b> CV curves of Na<sub>0.612</sub>K<sub>0.056</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub>, HC and the full battery of HC//Na<sub>0.612</sub>K<sub>0.056</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> at 0.1 mV s<sup>−1</sup>. <b>f</b> Typical charge/discharge curves of HC//Na<sub>0.612</sub>K<sub>0.056</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> at 50 mA g<sup>−1</sup>.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41467-021-22523-3/figures/6" data-track-dest="link:Figure6 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 6" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>The cycle stability of Na<sub>0.612</sub>K<sub>0.056</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> is tested at 50 mA g<sup>−1</sup>, and the selected charge/discharge profiles of the 1st, 5th, 10th, and 100th cycles are presented in Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-021-22523-3#MOESM1">32</a>. Except for the 1st charge, the charge/discharge profiles are almost overlapped. The capacity after 100 cycles is sustained for 236.2 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, corresponding to capacity retention of 98.2% with only 0.018% loss per cycle in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-021-22523-3#Fig6">6c</a>, which is highly contrasting with the fluctuating capacities of Na<sub>0.706</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub>. This implies that the structure of Na<sub>0.612</sub>K<sub>0.056</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> is robust upon extraction and insertion of Na<sup>+</sup> in cycles, as confirmed by in situ XRD in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-021-22523-3#Fig3">3</a>.</p><p>The Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficients are estimated by Galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) in Supplementary Figs.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-021-22523-3#MOESM1">33</a>–<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-021-22523-3#MOESM1">37</a>. The obtained diffusion coefficients (<i>D</i><sub>Na</sub>+) for the single-phase regions of both Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>K<sub>0.056</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> and Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> are in the range of 10<sup>−12</sup>–10<sup>−10</sup> cm<sup>2</sup>s<sup>−1</sup>, and they exhibit decreasing trends as the sodiation proceeds near the two-phase regions in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-021-22523-3#Fig6">6d</a> and Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-021-22523-3#MOESM1">38</a>. Because the GITT method cannot be applicable to the two-phase regions, CVs at different scan rates are used to calculate the apparent values of <i>D</i><sub>Na+</sub> in Na<sub>0.612</sub>K<sub>0.056</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> and Na<sub>0.706</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub>, as presented in the gray region in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-021-22523-3#Fig6">6d</a>, Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-021-22523-3#MOESM1">39</a>, and Supplementary Table&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-021-22523-3#MOESM1">19</a>. Na<sub>0.612</sub>K<sub>0.056</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> exhibits faster Na<sup>+</sup> transport with the content change of Na during charge and discharge, though there is K<sup>+</sup> riveted between the layers. Enhanced rate capability is presented in Na<sub>0.612</sub>K<sub>0.056</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> in Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-021-22523-3#MOESM1">40</a>, in which the reversible capacities are kept from 238.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> to 211.6 and 110.2 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at the currents from 50 mA g<sup>−1</sup> to 100 and 2000 mA g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. The demonstrated good cycle performance and rate capability of Na<sub>0.612</sub>K<sub>0.056</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> are attributed to the reinforced structure stability and facile Na<sup>+</sup> transport.</p><p>A full battery with P2-Na<sub>0.612</sub>K<sub>0.056</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> cathode and presodiated hard carbon (HC) anode was demonstrated. The performance of HC anode was firstly investigated in half battery in Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-021-22523-3#MOESM1">41a</a>. As displayed in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-021-22523-3#Fig6">6e</a>, a pair of redox peaks appear at 0.036/0.113 V for HC anode, and the obtained peaks of the full battery are similar to those of Na<sub>0.612</sub>K<sub>0.056</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub>, implying reversible electrochemical reactions. The full battery delivers a specific capacity of 230.6 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> based on the mass of active cathode material at 50 mA g<sup>−1</sup> in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-021-22523-3#Fig6">6f</a>, corresponding to a high energy density of 314.4 Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> based on the total mass of active anode and cathode materials. It also exhibits good cycling stability and rate performance in Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-021-22523-3#MOESM1">41</a>. The electrochemical performance can be optimized by selecting high efficient HC and Na compensation method. This implies that P2-Na<sub>0.612</sub>K<sub>0.056</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> will be of great potential for the high-performance SIBs.</p><p>In summary, a cathode material of P2-Na<sub>0.612</sub>K<sub>0.056</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> has been successfully obtained with the K<sup>+</sup> riveted in the prismatic edge-sharing sites of Na<sub>e</sub> between the MnO<sub>6</sub>-octahedra slabs. The reinforced MnO<sub>6</sub>-octahedra slabs and reduced Na<sup>+</sup> vacancy formation energy enable more active Na<sup>+</sup> sites and favor its facile diffusion. This leads to the highest reversible capacity of 240.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, corresponding to 0.901 Na<sup>+</sup> per formula, and energy density of 654 Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> based on the redox of Mn<sup>3+</sup>/Mn<sup>4+</sup> among the reported transition-metal oxide cathodes for SIBs, and good capacity retention of 98.2% after 100 cycles. The reinforced interaction in the MnO<sub>6</sub>-octahedra slabs restricts the layer gliding and ensures the robust crystal structure of P2-Na<sub>0.612</sub>K<sub>0.056</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub>, in which two-phase transition of P2 ↔ P’2 occurs only at low charge and discharge voltages, favoring the structure stability and cycle performance. This strategy to finely tune the local chemistry for high energy density and long cycle life will shed lights into the design of electrode materials for SIBs and beyond.</p></div></div></section><section data-title="Methods"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec6-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec6">Methods</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec6-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec7">Materials synthesis</h3><p>P2-Na<sub>0.67-<i>x</i></sub>K<sub><i>x</i></sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> was synthesized via a solid-state reaction. For the synthesis of Na<sub>0.612</sub>K<sub>0.056</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub>, NaCH<sub>3</sub>COOH (99%, Alfa, 12.54 mmol, 10% in excess), K<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> (99%, Alfa, 2.1 mmol, 5% in excess), and MnO<sub>2</sub> (99%, Alfa, 20 mmol) were mixed in a planetary ball mill (QM-3SP2) at 400 rpm for 12 h in the presence of a small amount of acetone. The as-synthesized precursors were dried at 80 °C for 12 h, and then pressed into a pallet under 20 MPa. It was heated at 500 °C for 2 h and 900 °C for 10 h in air at 5 °C/min. Then, it was cooled down to 200 °C at 5 °C/min and naturally to room temperature, and stored in an argon-filled glovebox. Similar processes were applicable to the synthesis of Na<sub>0.706</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> except the addition of K<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec8">Electrochemical measurements</h3><p>Coin cells (CR2032) were assembled in an argon-filled glovebox for all the electrochemical tests. The working electrode was prepared by coating the mixture of active material (80 wt.%), Super P (10 wt.%), and polytetrafluoroethylene (10 wt.%) in <i>N</i>-methyl-2-pyrrolidone onto an Al foil. The loading mass of active material in each electrode pellet of 12.0 mm in diameter was ~3.0 mg cm<sup>−2</sup>. For half battery, sodium foil was used as the anode, and 1.0 M NaPF<sub>6</sub> in PC containing 5 wt.% of FEC was employed as the electrolyte with glass fiber filter papers as the separator. The charge/discharge tests and Galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) were carried out on a Land CT2001A battery test system (Land, Wuhan, China) in a voltage range of 1.8–4.3 V at 25 °C. GITT was measured by applying the repeated current pulses for 30 min at a current density of 10 mA g<sup>−1</sup>, followed by relaxation for 1.5 h. CV experiments were performed within the same potential range at 0.1 mV s<sup>−</sup><sup>1</sup>. CV was carried out on a Solartron 1470E electrochemical workstation in a voltage range of 1.8–4.3 V. The full battery was assembled with P2-Na<sub>0.612</sub>K<sub>0.056</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> as the cathode, HC as the anode, and 1.0 M NaPF<sub>6</sub> in PC containing 5 wt.% of FEC as the electrolyte, respectively. In order to supplement sufficient Na<sup>+</sup> in HC before assembling full battery, the HC electrode was obtained by disassembling the half battery in the glove box after half-discharging at 50 mA g<sup>−1</sup>. The mass ratio of Na<sub>0.612</sub>K<sub>0.056</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub>/HC is around 1.2, corresponding to 4% excess of anode capacity. The charge/discharge and CV tests were carried out at 25 °C in a voltage range of 1.0–4.3 V.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec9">Material characterizations</h3><p>The chemical composition of the electrodes was determined by an inductively coupled plasma-optical emission spectrometer (ICP-OES, SPECTRO-BLUE). XRD was collected on Rigaku SmartLab equipped with a Cu Kα radiation source. Rietveld refinement was conducted with the Fullprof software<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 46" title="Rodríguez-Carvajal, J. Recent advances in magnetic structure determination by neutron powder diffraction. Phys. B Condens. Matter 192, 55–69 (1993)." href="/articles/s41467-021-22523-3#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d1718850e2652">46</a></sup>. The PDF analysis was carried out based on X-ray scattering data measured at the 11-ID-B beamline of the Advanced Photon Source at Argonne National Laboratory. High energy X-rays (<i>λ</i> = 0.1173 Å) were used to collect data to high values of momentum transfer (<i>Q</i> ~ 30 Å<sup>−1</sup>). Diffraction images were integrated within fit2D to obtain one-dimensional diffraction data<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 47" title="Hammersley, A. P. Fit2D version 9.129 reference manual version 3.1,&nbsp;ESRF Inter. Rep.&nbsp;No. ESRF98HA01T (1998)." href="/articles/s41467-021-22523-3#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d1718850e2664">47</a></sup>. Pair distribution functions, <i>G</i>(r), were extracted from the data within PDFgetX3<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="Juhás, P. et al. PDFgetX3: a rapid and highly automatable program for processing powder diffraction data into total scattering pair distribution functions. J. Appl. Crystallogr. 46, 560–566 (2013)." href="/articles/s41467-021-22523-3#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d1718850e2672">48</a></sup>, after correcting for background and Compton scattering. Mn K-edge X-ray absorption fine structure (XAFS) results were collected at the beamline 8C in Pohang Accelerator Laboratory (PAL). The XAFS data were collected by fluorescence mode and processed through Demeter software package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Ravel, B. &amp; Newville, M. ATHENA, ARTEMIS, HEPHAESTUS: data analysis for X-ray absorption spectroscopy using IFEFFIT. J. Synchrotron. Radiat. 12, 537–541 (2005)." href="/articles/s41467-021-22523-3#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d1718850e2676">49</a></sup>. The extended x-ray absorption fine structure (EXAFS) region was <i>k</i><sup>3</sup> weighted and Fourier-transformed in <i>k</i>-ranges of 3.0–10.0 Å<sup>−1</sup>. Schematic representations of the synthesized samples were obtained by using the VESTA software<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 50" title="Momma, K. &amp; Izumi, F. VESTA 3 for three-dimensional visualization of crystal, volumetric and morphology data. J. Appl. Crystallogr. 44, 1272–1276 (2011)." href="/articles/s41467-021-22523-3#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d1718850e2690">50</a></sup>. The morphology was examined by SEM (JEOL JSM-7500F, AEMC, 5 kV). The HRTEM images, SAED patterns and EDS mappings were recorded by TEM (FEI Taosl F200X G2, AEMC, 200 kV). HAADF and ABF images were obtained on a JEM-AR200F STEM with an accelerating voltage of 200 kV with cold filed-emission gun and double hexapole Cs correctors (CEOS GmbH, Heidelberg, Germany). Dynamic secondary ion mass spectroscopy (SIMS) was carried out on a Cameca IMS-5FE7 system using Cs<sup>+</sup> primary ions with a beam current of 3 nA. Solid-state <sup>39</sup>K NMR spectra were obtained on a JNM-ECZ600R widebore spectrometer.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec10">DFT calculation</h3><p>The crystal structures of Na<sub>0.500</sub>K<sub>0.055</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub>, Na<sub>0.220</sub>K<sub>0.055</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub>, and Na<sub>0.275</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> were simulated using Vienna ab-initio simulation package (VASP). The generalized gradient approximation (GGA) of exchange-correlation energy, Perdew-Burke-Eznerhof (PBE) functional, was used with its corresponding projector augmented-wave pseudopotentials<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Perdew, J. P., Burke, K. &amp; Ernzerhof, M. Generalized gradient approximation made simple. Phys. Rev. Lett. 77, 3865–3868 (1996)." href="#ref-CR31" id="ref-link-section-d1718850e2723">31</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Kresse, G. &amp; Furthmüller, J. Efficient iterative schemes for ab initio total-energy calculations using a plane-wave basis set. J. Phys. Rev. B 54, 11169–11186 (1996)." href="#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d1718850e2723_1">32</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Blöchl, P. E. Projector augmented-wave method. Phys. Rev. B 50, 17953–17979 (1994)." href="#ref-CR33" id="ref-link-section-d1718850e2723_2">33</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 34" title="Kresse, G. &amp; Joubert, D. From ultrasoft pseudopotentials to the projector augmented-wave method. Phys. Rev. B 59, 1758–1775 (1999)." href="/articles/s41467-021-22523-3#ref-CR34" id="ref-link-section-d1718850e2726">34</a></sup>. A Hubbard <i>U</i> term of 3.9 is adopted to better describe the strong correlation of Mn 3<i>d</i> electrons. The slight difference between the simulated formulas and the obtained composition is due to that the number of K and Na atoms can only be integral in a unit cell, and such difference can be reasonably ignored. All optimization calculations adopted a 4 × 4 × 4 Monkhorst-Pack<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Monkhorst, H. J. &amp; Pack, J. D. Special points for brillonin-zone integrations. Phys. Rev. B 13, 5188–5192 (1976)." href="/articles/s41467-021-22523-3#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d1718850e2737">51</a></sup> k-point grid and a cutoff energy of 400 eV, and a higher cutoff of 450 eV and a 6 × 6 × 4 k-point grid were applied for DOS and charge calculations for enhanced accuracy. First-principle molecular dynamics calculations, which adopt an NVT ensemble at 1000 K, were carried out using a single Γ point to balance the accuracy and cost. Atomic positions and cell vectors were fully optimized until all force components were less than 0.02 eV Å<sup>−1</sup>. The trajectory of MD simulation was further analyzed using Rigorous Investigation of Networks Generated using Simulations (R.I.N.G.S.) code to obtain MSD statistics. The COHP calculations were carried out using Local-Orbital Basis Suite towards Electronic-Structure Reconstruction (LOBSTER) code. The diffusion energy barriers are calculated using climbing-image nudged elastic band (CI-NEB) method with a single Γ point.</p></div></div></section>
                    
                </div>

                                <p class="c-article-further-reading__journal-title"><i>Journal of Electronic Materials</i> (2025)</p>
                            </li>
                        
                            <li class="c-article-further-reading__item js-ref-item">
                            
                                <h3 class="c-article-further-reading__title" data-test="article-title">

                                        Designing neighboring-site activation of single atom via tunnel ions for boosting acidic oxygen evolution
                                    </a>
                                </h3>

                                    </ul>
                                
                                <p class="c-article-further-reading__journal-title"><i>Nature Communications</i> (2024)</p>
                            </li>

                                    </a>
